   [1m[7mBrace[27m[0m [1mExpansion[0m[m
       [4m[7mBrace[27m[24m [4mexpansion[24m is a mechanism by which arbitrary strings may be generated.  This  mecha‚Äê[m
       nism  is similar to [4mpathname[24m [4mexpansion[24m, but the filenames generated need not exist.  Pat‚Äê[m
       terns to be brace expanded take the form of an optional [4mpreamble[24m, followed  by  either  a[m
       series of comma-separated strings or a sequence expression between a pair of braces, fol‚Äê[m
       lowed by an optional [4mpostscript[24m.  The preamble  is  prefixed  to  each  string  contained[m
       within  the braces, and the postscript is then appended to each resulting string, expand‚Äê[m
       ing left to right.[m
[m
       [7mBrace[27m expansions may be nested.  The results of each expanded string are not sorted; left[m
       to right order is preserved.  For example, a[1m{[0md,c,b[1m}[0me expands into `ade ace abe'.[m
[m
       A sequence expression takes the form [1m{[0m[4mx[24m[1m..[0m[4my[24m[1m[..[0m[4mincr[24m[1m]}[0m, where [4mx[24m and [4my[24m are either integers or[m
       single letters, and [4mincr[24m, an optional increment, is an integer.  When integers  are  sup‚Äê[m
       plied,  the expression expands to each number between [4mx[24m and [4my[24m, inclusive.  Supplied inte‚Äê[m
       gers may be prefixed with [4m0[24m to force each term to have the same width.  When either [4mx[24m  or[m
       [4my[24m begins with a zero, the shell attempts to force all generated terms to contain the same[m
       number of digits, zero-padding where necessary.  When letters are supplied,  the  expres‚Äê[m
       sion  expands  to  each character lexicographically between [4mx[24m and [4my[24m, inclusive, using the[m
       default C locale.  Note that both [4mx[24m and [4my[24m must be of the same type (integer  or  letter).[m
       When  the increment is supplied, it is used as the difference between each term.  The de‚Äê[m
       fault increment is 1 or -1 as appropriate.[m
[m
       [7mBrace[27m expansion is performed before any other expansions, and any characters  special  to[m

[m
       [7mBrace[27m expansions may be nested.  The results of each expanded string are not sorted; left[m
       to right order is preserved.  For example, a[1m{[0md,c,b[1m}[0me expands into `ade ace abe'.[m
[m
       A sequence expression takes the form [1m{[0m[4mx[24m[1m..[0m[4my[24m[1m[..[0m[4mincr[24m[1m]}[0m, where [4mx[24m and [4my[24m are either integers or[m
       single letters, and [4mincr[24m, an optional increment, is an integer.  When integers  are  sup‚Äê[m
       plied,  the expression expands to each number between [4mx[24m and [4my[24m, inclusive.  Supplied inte‚Äê[m
       gers may be prefixed with [4m0[24m to force each term to have the same width.  When either [4mx[24m  or[m
       [4my[24m begins with a zero, the shell attempts to force all generated terms to contain the same[m
       number of digits, zero-padding where necessary.  When letters are supplied,  the  expres‚Äê[m
       sion  expands  to  each character lexicographically between [4mx[24m and [4my[24m, inclusive, using the[m
       default C locale.  Note that both [4mx[24m and [4my[24m must be of the same type (integer  or  letter).[m
       When  the increment is supplied, it is used as the difference between each term.  The de‚Äê[m
       fault increment is 1 or -1 as appropriate.[m
[m
       [7mBrace[27m expansion is performed before any other expansions, and any characters  special  to[m
       other expansions are preserved in the result.  It is strictly textual.  [1mBash[0m does not ap‚Äê[m
       ply any syntactic interpretation to the context of the expansion or the text between  the[m
       braces.[m
[m
       A  correctly-formed brace expansion must contain unquoted opening and closing braces, and[m
       at least one unquoted comma or a valid sequence expression.  Any incorrectly formed brace[m

[1mSYNOPSIS[0m[m
[m
       [1msystemctl [22m[OPTIONS...] COMMAND [UNIT...][m
[m
[1mDESCRIPTION[0m[m
       [1msystemctl [22mmay be used to introspect and control the state of the "systemd" system and[m
       service manager. Please refer to [1msystemd[22m(1) for an introduction into the basic concepts[m
       and functionality this tool manages.[m
[m
[1mCOMMANDS[0m[m
       The following commands are understood:[m
[m
   [1mUnit Commands (Introspection and Modification)[0m[m
       [1mlist-units [22m[[4mPATTERN[24m...][m
           List units that [1msystemd [22mcurrently has in memory. This includes units that are either[m
           referenced directly or through a dependency, units that are pinned by applications[m
[7m Manual page systemctl(1) line 1 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K           programmatically, or units that were active in the past and have failed. By default[m
           only units which are active, have pending jobs, or have failed are shown; this can be[m
           changed with option [1m--all[22m. If one or more [4mPATTERN[24ms are specified, only units matching[m
           one of them are shown. The units that are shown are additionally filtered by [1m--type=[0m[m
           and [1m--state= [22mif those options are specified.[m
[m
           Note that this command does not show unit templates, but only instances of unit[m
           templates. Units templates that aren't instantiated are not runnable, and will thus[m
           never show up in the output of this command. Specifically this means that[m
           foo@.service will never be shown in this list ‚Äî unless instantiated, e.g. as[m
           foo@bar.service. Use [1mlist-unit-files [22m(see below) for listing installed unit template[m
           files.[m
[m
           Produces output similar to[m
[m
                 UNIT                         LOAD   ACTIVE SUB     DESCRIPTION[m
                 sys-module-fuse.device       loaded active plugged /sys/module/fuse[m
                 -.mount                      loaded active mounted Root Mount[m
                 boot-efi.mount               loaded active mounted /boot/efi[m
                 systemd-journald.service     loaded active running Journal Service[m
                 systemd-logind.service       loaded active running Login Service[m
[7m Manual page systemctl(1) line 22 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K[?1l>[?1049l[23;0;0t[?2004h]0;user@ubse: ~[01;32muser@ubse[00m:[01;34m~[00m$ [H[2J]0;user@ubse: ~[01;32muser@ubse[00m:[01;34m~[00m$ man systemctl sudo systemctl list-units^C[?2004l[?2004h[?2004l

[?2004l[?1049h[22;0;0t[?1h=[4mSYSTEMCTL[24m(1)                                systemctl                               [4mSYSTEMCTL[24m(1)[m
[m
[1mNAME[0m[m
       systemctl - Control the systemd system and service manager[m
[m
[1mSYNOPSIS[0m[m
[m
       [1msystemctl [22m[OPTIONS...] COMMAND [UNIT...][m
[m
[1mDESCRIPTION[0m[m
       [1msystemctl [22mmay be used to introspect and control the state of the "systemd" system and[m
       service manager. Please refer to [1msystemd[22m(1) for an introduction into the basic concepts[m
       and functionality this tool manages.[m
[m
[1mCOMMANDS[0m[m
       The following commands are understood:[m
[m
   [1mUnit Commands (Introspection and Modification)[0m[m
       [1mlist-units [22m[[4mPATTERN[24m...][m
           List units that [1msystemd [22mcurrently has in memory. This includes units that are either[m
[7m Manual page systemctl(1) line 1 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K           referenced directly or through a dependency, units that are pinned by applications[m
           programmatically, or units that were active in the past and have failed. By default[m
           only units which are active, have pending jobs, or have failed are shown; this can be[m
           changed with option [1m--all[22m. If one or more [4mPATTERN[24ms are specified, only units matching[m
           one of them are shown. The units that are shown are additionally filtered by [1m--type=[0m[m
           and [1m--state= [22mif those options are specified.[m
[m
           Note that this command does not show unit templates, but only instances of unit[m
           templates. Units templates that aren't instantiated are not runnable, and will thus[m
           never show up in the output of this command. Specifically this means that[m
           foo@.service will never be shown in this list ‚Äî unless instantiated, e.g. as[m
           foo@bar.service. Use [1mlist-unit-files [22m(see below) for listing installed unit template[m
           files.[m
[m
           Produces output similar to[m
[m
                 UNIT                         LOAD   ACTIVE SUB     DESCRIPTION[m
                 sys-module-fuse.device       loaded active plugged /sys/module/fuse[m
                 -.mount                      loaded active mounted Root Mount[m
                 boot-efi.mount               loaded active mounted /boot/efi[m
[7m Manual page systemctl(1) line 21 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[Kset mark: [K[7mInvalid mark letter    (press RETURN)[27m[21;1H[K...skipping...
           referenced directly or through a dependency, units that are pinned by applications[m
           programmatically, or units that were active in the past and have failed. By default[m
           only units which are active, have pending jobs, or have failed are shown; this can be[m
           changed with option [1m--all[22m. If one or more [4mPATTERN[24ms are specified, only units matching[m
           one of them are shown. The units that are shown are additionally filtered by [1m--type=[0m[m
           and [1m--state= [22mif those options are specified.[m
[m
           Note that this command does not show unit templates, but only instances of unit[m
           templates. Units templates that aren't instantiated are not runnable, and will thus[m
           never show up in the output of this command. Specifically this means that[m
           foo@.service will never be shown in this list ‚Äî unless instantiated, e.g. as[m
           foo@bar.service. Use [1mlist-unit-files [22m(see below) for listing installed unit template[m
           files.[m
[m
           Produces output similar to[m
[m
                 UNIT                         LOAD   ACTIVE SUB     DESCRIPTION[m
                 sys-module-fuse.device       loaded active plugged /sys/module/fuse[m
                 -.mount                      loaded active mounted Root Mount[m
                 boot-efi.mount               loaded active mounted /boot/efi[m
[7m Manual page systemctl(1) line 21 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K                 systemd-journald.service     loaded active running Journal Service[m
                 systemd-logind.service       loaded active running Login Service[m
               ‚óè user@1000.service            loaded failed failed  User Manager for UID 1000[m
                 ...[m
                 systemd-tmpfiles-clean.timer loaded active waiting Daily Cleanup of Temporary Dire[m ctories[m
[m
               LOAD   = Reflects whether the unit definition was properly loaded.[m
               ACTIVE = The high-level unit activation state, i.e. generalization of SUB.[m
               SUB    = The low-level unit activation state, values depend on unit type.[m
[m
               123 loaded units listed. Pass --all to see loaded but inactive units, too.[m
               To show all installed unit files use 'systemctl list-unit-files'.[m
[m
           The header and the last unit of a given type are underlined if the terminal supports[m
           that. A colored dot is shown next to services which were masked, not found, or[m
           otherwise failed.[m
[m
           The LOAD column shows the load state, one of [1mloaded[22m, [1mnot-found[22m, [1mbad-setting[22m, [1merror[22m,[m
           [1mmasked[22m. The ACTIVE columns shows the general unit state, one of [1mactive[22m, [1mreloading[22m,[m
[7m Manual page systemctl(1) line 41 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K           [1minactive[22m, [1mfailed[22m, [1mactivating[22m, [1mdeactivating[22m. The SUB column shows the[m
           unit-type-specific detailed state of the unit, possible values vary by unit type. The[m
           list of possible LOAD, ACTIVE, and SUB states is not constant and new systemd[m
           releases may both add and remove values.[m
[m
               systemctl --state=help[m
[m
           command may be used to display the current set of possible values.[m
[m
           This is the default command.[m
[m

               systemctl --state=help[m

       [1mlist-paths [22m[[4mPATTERN[24m...][m
           List path units currently in memory, ordered by path. If one or more [4mPATTERN[24ms are[m
           specified, only path units matching one of them are shown. Produces output similar to[m
[m
               PATH                           CONDITION         UNIT                               [m ACTIVATES[m
               /run/systemd/ask-password      DirectoryNotEmpty systemd-ask-password-plymouth.path [m systemd-ask-password-plymouth.service[m
               /run/systemd/ask-password      DirectoryNotEmpty systemd-ask-password-wall.path     [m systemd-ask-password-wall.service[m
               /var/cache/cups/org.cups.cupsd PathExists        cups.path                          [m cups.service[m
[m
[7m Manual page systemctl(1) line 79 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K               3 paths listed.[m
[m
           Also see [1m--show-types[22m, [1m--all[22m, and [1m--state=[22m.[m
[m
           Added in version 254.[m
[m
       [1mlist-sockets [22m[[4mPATTERN[24m...][m
           List socket units currently in memory, ordered by listening address. If one or more[m
           [4mPATTERN[24ms are specified, only socket units matching one of them are shown. Produces[m
           output similar to[m
[m
               LISTEN           UNIT                        ACTIVATES[m
               /dev/initctl     systemd-initctl.socket      systemd-initctl.service[m
               ...[m
               [::]:22          sshd.socket                 sshd.service[m
               kobject-uevent 1 systemd-udevd-kernel.socket systemd-udevd.service[m
[m
               5 sockets listed.[m
[m
           Note: because the addresses might contains spaces, this output is not suitable for[m
[7m Manual page systemctl(1) line 95 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K           programmatic consumption.[m
[m
           Also see [1m--show-types[22m, [1m--all[22m, and [1m--state=[22m.[m
[m
           Added in version 202.[m
[m
       [1mlist-timers [22m[[4mPATTERN[24m...][m
           List timer units currently in memory, ordered by the time they elapse next. If one or[m
           more [4mPATTERN[24ms are specified, only units matching one of them are shown. Produces[m
           output similar to[m
[m
               NEXT                         LEFT          LAST                         PASSED     U[m NIT                         ACTIVATES[m
               -                            -             Thu 2017-02-23 13:40:29 EST  3 days ago u[m readahead-stop.timer        ureadahead-stop.service[m
               Sun 2017-02-26 18:55:42 EST  1min 14s left Thu 2017-02-23 13:54:44 EST  3 days ago s[m ystemd-tmpfiles-clean.timer systemd-tmpfiles-clean.service[m
               Sun 2017-02-26 20:37:16 EST  1h 42min left Sun 2017-02-26 11:56:36 EST  6h ago     a[m pt-daily.timer              apt-daily.service[m
               Sun 2017-02-26 20:57:49 EST  2h 3min left  Sun 2017-02-26 11:56:36 EST  6h ago     s[m [7m Manual page systemctl(1) line 115 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[Knapd.refresh.timer          snapd.refresh.service[m
[m
           [4mNEXT[24m shows the next time the timer will run.[m
[m
           [4mLEFT[24m shows how long till the next time the timer runs.[m
[m
           [4mLAST[24m shows the last time the timer ran.[m
[m
           [4mPASSED[24m shows how long has passed since the timer last ran.[m
[m
           [4mUNIT[24m shows the name of the timer[m
[m
           [4mACTIVATES[24m shows the name the service the timer activates when it runs.[m
[m
           Also see [1m--all [22mand [1m--state=[22m.[m
[m
           Added in version 209.[m
[m
       [1mis-active [4m[22mPATTERN[24m[1m...[0m[m
           Check whether any of the specified units are active (i.e. running). Returns an exit[m
[7m Manual page systemctl(1) line 130 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K           code [1m0 [22mif at least one is active, or non-zero otherwise. Unless [1m--quiet [22mis specified,[m
           this will also print the current unit state to standard output.[m
[m
       [1mis-failed [[4m[22mPATTERN[24m...][m
           Check whether any of the specified units is in the "failed" state. If no unit is[m
           specified, check whether there are any failed units, which corresponds to the[m
           "degraded" state returned by [1mis-system-running[22m. Returns an exit code [1m0 [22mif at least[m
           one has failed, non-zero otherwise. Unless [1m--quiet [22mis specified, this will also print[m
           the current unit or system state to standard output.[m
[m
           Added in version 197.[m
[m
       [1mstatus [22m[[4mPATTERN[24m...|[4mPID[24m...]][m
           Show runtime status information about the whole system or about one or more units[m
           followed by most recent log data from the journal. If no positional arguments are[m
           specified, and no unit filter is given with [1m--type=[22m, [1m--state=[22m, or [1m--failed[22m, shows the[m
           status of the whole system. If combined with [1m--all[22m, follows that with the status of[m
           all units. If positional arguments are specified, each positional argument is treated[m
           as either a unit name to show, or a glob pattern to show units whose names match that[m
           pattern, or a PID to show the unit containing that PID. When [1m--type=[22m, [1m--state=[22m, or[m
[7m Manual page systemctl(1) line 150 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K           [1m--failed [22mare used, units are additionally filtered by the TYPE and ACTIVE state.[m
[m
           This function is intended to generate human-readable output. If you are looking for[m
           computer-parsable output, use [1mshow [22minstead. By default, this function only shows 10[m
           lines of output and ellipsizes lines to fit in the terminal window. This can be[m
           changed with [1m--lines [22mand [1m--full[22m, see above. In addition, [1mjournalctl --unit=[4m[22mNAME[24m or[m
           [1mjournalctl --user-unit=[4m[22mNAME[24m use a similar filter for messages and might be more[m
           convenient.[m
[m
           Note that this operation only displays [4mruntime[24m status, i.e. information about the[m
           current invocation of the unit (if it is running) or the most recent invocation (if[m
           it is not running anymore, and has not been released from memory). Information about[m
           earlier invocations, invocations from previous system boots, or prior invocations[m
           that have already been released from memory may be retrieved via [1mjournalctl --unit=[22m.[m
[m
           systemd implicitly loads units as necessary, so just running the [1mstatus [22mwill attempt[m
           to load a file. The command is thus not useful for determining if something was[m
           already loaded or not. The units may possibly also be quickly unloaded after the[m
           operation is completed if there's no reason to keep it in memory thereafter.[m
[m

[m
[1mNAME[0m[m
       systemctl - Control the systemd system and service manager[m
[m
[1mSYNOPSIS[0m[m
[m
       [1msystemctl [22m[OPTIONS...] COMMAND [UNIT...][m
[m
[1mDESCRIPTION[0m[m
       [1msystemctl [22mmay be used to introspect and control the state of the "systemd" system and[m
       service manager. Please refer to [1msystemd[22m(1) for an introduction into the basic concepts[m
       and functionality this tool manages.[m
[m
[1mCOMMANDS[0m[m
       The following commands are understood:[m
[m
   [1mUnit Commands (Introspection and Modification)[0m[m
       [1mlist-units [22m[[4mPATTERN[24m...][m
           List units that [1msystemd [22mcurrently has in memory. This includes units that are either[m
[7m Manual page systemctl(1) line 1 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K[?1l>[?1049l[23;0;0t[?2004h]0;root@ubse: ~root@ubse:~# fg
[?2004lman systemctl
[?1049h[22;0;0t[?1h=[H[2J[H           some way, such as a crash, exiting with an error code or timing out. If the failed[m
           state is entered the cause will be logged for later reference.[m
[m
       [1mshow [22m[[4mPATTERN[24m...|[4mJOB[24m...][m
           Show properties of one or more units, jobs, or the manager itself. If no argument is[m
           specified, properties of the manager will be shown. If a unit name is specified,[m
           properties of the unit are shown, and if a job ID is specified, properties of the job[m
           are shown. By default, empty properties are suppressed. Use [1m--all [22mto show those too.[m
           To select specific properties to show, use [1m--property=[22m. This command is intended to[m
           be used whenever computer-parsable output is required. Use [1mstatus [22mif you are looking[m
           for formatted human-readable output.[m
[m
           Many properties shown by [1msystemctl show [22mmap directly to configuration settings of the[m
           system and service manager and its unit files. Note that the properties shown by the[m
           command are generally more low-level, normalized versions of the original[m
           configuration settings and expose runtime state in addition to configuration. For[m
           example, properties shown for service units include the service's current main[m
           process identifier as "MainPID" (which is runtime state), and time settings are[m
           always exposed as properties ending in the "...USec" suffix even if a matching[m
           configuration options end in "...Sec", because microseconds is the normalized time[m
[7m Manual page systemctl(1) line 229 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K           unit used internally by the system and service manager.[m

       [1misolate [4m[22mUNIT[0m[m
           Start the unit specified on the command line and its dependencies and stop all[m
           others, unless they have [1mIgnoreOnIsolate=yes [22m(see [1msystemd.unit[22m(5)). If a unit name[m
           with no extension is given, an extension of ".target" will be assumed.[m
[m
           This command is dangerous, since it will immediately stop processes that are not[m
           enabled in the new target, possibly including the graphical environment or terminal[m
           you are currently using.[m
[m
           Note that this operation is allowed only on units where [1mAllowIsolate= [22mis enabled. See[m
           [1msystemd.unit[22m(5) for details.[m
[7m Manual page systemctl(1) line 352 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K[m

           select which process to send the signal to. Use [1m--signal= [22mto select the signal to[m

       [1mclean [4m[22mPATTERN[24m[1m...[0m[m
           Remove the configuration, state, cache, logs or runtime data of the specified units.[m
           Use [1m--what= [22mto select which kind of resource to remove. For service units this may be[m
           used to remove the directories configured with [4mConfigurationDirectory=[24m,[m
           [4mStateDirectory=[24m, [4mCacheDirectory=[24m, [4mLogsDirectory=[24m and [4mRuntimeDirectory=[24m, see[m
           [1msystemd.exec[22m(5) for details. It may also be used to clear the file descriptor store[m
           as enabled via [4mFileDescriptorStoreMax=[24m, see [1msystemd.service[22m(5) for details. For timer[m
[7m Manual page systemctl(1) line 366 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K           units this may be used to clear out the persistent timestamp data if [4mPersistent=[24m is[m
           used and [1m--what=state [22mis selected, see [1msystemd.timer[22m(5). This command only applies to[m
           units that use either of these settings. If [1m--what= [22mis not specified, the cache and[m
           runtime data as well as the file descriptor store are removed (as these three types[m
           of resources are generally redundant and reproducible on the next invocation of the[m
           unit). Note that the specified units must be stopped to invoke this operation.[m
[m
           Added in version 243.[m
[m
       [1mfreeze [4m[22mPATTERN[24m[1m...[0m[m
           Freeze one or more units specified on the command line using cgroup freezer[m
[m
           Freezing the unit will cause all processes contained within the cgroup corresponding[m
           to the unit to be suspended. Being suspended means that unit's processes won't be[m
[7m Manual page systemctl(1) line 380 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K           scheduled to run on CPU until thawed. Note that this command is supported only on[m
           systems that use unified cgroup hierarchy. Unit is automatically thawed just before[m
           we execute a job against the unit, e.g. before the unit is stopped.[m
[m
           Added in version 246.[m
[m
       [1mthaw [4m[22mPATTERN[24m[1m...[0m[m
           Thaw (unfreeze) one or more units specified on the command line.[m
[m
           This is the inverse operation to the [1mfreeze [22mcommand and resumes the execution of[m
           processes in the unit's cgroup.[m
[m
           Added in version 246.[m
[m
[7m Manual page systemctl(1) line 394 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K       [1mset-property [4m[22mUNIT[24m [4mPROPERTY[24m[1m=[4m[22mVALUE[24m[1m...[0m[m
           Set the specified unit properties at runtime where this is supported. This allows[m
           changing configuration parameter properties such as resource control settings at[m
           runtime. Not all properties may be changed at runtime, but many resource control[m
           settings (primarily those in [1msystemd.resource-control[22m(5)) may. The changes are[m
           applied immediately, and stored on disk for future boots, unless [1m--runtime [22mis passed,[m
           in which case the settings only apply until the next reboot. The syntax of the[m
           property assignment follows closely the syntax of assignments in unit files.[m
[m
           Example: [1msystemctl set-property foobar.service CPUWeight=200[0m[m
[m
           If the specified unit appears to be inactive, the changes will be only stored on disk[m
           as described previously hence they will be effective when the unit will be started.[m
[m
[7m Manual page systemctl(1) line 408 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K           Note that this command allows changing multiple properties at the same time, which is[m
           preferable over setting them individually.[m
[m
           Example: [1msystemctl set-property foobar.service CPUWeight=200 MemoryMax=2G[0m[m
           [1mIPAccounting=yes[0m[m
[m
           Like with unit file configuration settings, assigning an empty setting usually resets[m
           a property to its defaults.[m
[m
           Example: [1msystemctl set-property avahi-daemon.service IPAddressDeny=[0m[m
[m
           Added in version 206.[m

       [1mbind [4m[22mUNIT[24m [4mPATH[24m [[4mPATH[24m][m
[7m Manual page systemctl(1) line 422 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K           Bind-mounts a file or directory from the host into the specified unit's mount[m
           namespace. The first path argument is the source file or directory on the host, the[m
           second path argument is the destination file or directory in the unit's mount[m
           namespace. When the latter is omitted, the destination path in the unit's mount[m
           namespace is the same as the source path on the host. When combined with the[m
           [1m--read-only [22mswitch, a ready-only bind mount is created. When combined with the[m
           [1m--mkdir [22mswitch, the destination path is first created before the mount is applied.[m
[m
           Note that this option is currently only supported for units that run within a mount[m
           namespace (e.g.: with [1mRootImage=[22m, [1mPrivateMounts=[22m, etc.). This command supports[m
           bind-mounting directories, regular files, device nodes, [1mAF_UNIX [22msocket nodes, as well[m
           as FIFOs. The bind mount is ephemeral, and it is undone as soon as the current unit[m
           process exists. Note that the namespace mentioned here, where the bind mount will be[m
           added to, is the one where the main service process runs. Other processes (those[m
[7m Manual page systemctl(1) line 436 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K           exececuted by [1mExecReload=[22m, [1mExecStartPre=[22m, etc.) run in distinct namespaces.[m
[m
           If supported by the kernel, any prior mount on the selected target will be replaced[m
           by the new mount. If not supported, any prior mount will be over-mounted, but remain[m
           pinned and inaccessible.[m
[m
           Added in version 248.[m
[m
       [1mmount-image [4m[22mUNIT[24m [4mIMAGE[24m [[4mPATH[24m [[4mPARTITION_NAME[24m:[4mMOUNT_OPTIONS[24m]][m

[7m Manual page systemctl(1) line 450 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K           that partition. The format is the same as the service [1mMountImages= [22msetting. When[m
           combined with the [1m--read-only [22mswitch, a ready-only mount is created. When combined[m
           with the [1m--mkdir [22mswitch, the destination path is first created before the mount is[m
           applied.[m
[m
           Note that this option is currently only supported for units that run within a mount[m
           namespace (i.e. with [1mRootImage=[22m, [1mPrivateMounts=[22m, etc.). Note that the namespace[m
           mentioned here where the image mount will be added to, is the one where the main[m
           service process runs. Note that the namespace mentioned here, where the bind mount[m
           will be added to, is the one where the main service process runs. Other processes[m
           (those exececuted by [1mExecReload=[22m, [1mExecStartPre=[22m, etc.) run in distinct namespaces.[m
[m
           If supported by the kernel, any prior mount on the selected target will be replaced[m

[m

       [1m[7menable[27m[1m [4m[22mUNIT[24m[1m...[22m, [1m[7menable[27m[1m [4m[22mPATH[24m[1m...[0m[m
           [7mEnable[27m one or more units or unit instances. This will create a set of symlinks, as[m
           encoded in the [Install] sections of the indicated unit files. After the symlinks[m
           have been created, the system manager configuration is reloaded (in a way equivalent[m
[7m Manual page systemctl(1) line 551 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K/[K           to [1mdaemon-reload[22m), in order to ensure the changes are taken into account immediately.[m
[7m Manual page systemctl(1) line 552 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K/[K           Note that this does [4mnot[24m have the effect of also starting any of the units being[m
           [7menable[27md. If this is desired, combine this command with the [1m--now [22mswitch, or invoke[m
           [1mstart [22mwith appropriate arguments later. Note that in case of unit instance [7menable[27m[22mment[m
           (i.e. [7menable[27mment of units of the form foo@bar.service), symlinks named the same as[m
           instances are created in the unit configuration directory, however they point to the[m
           single template unit file they are instantiated from.[m
[m
           This command expects either valid unit names (in which case various unit file[m
           directories are automatically searched for unit files with appropriate names), or[m
[7m Manual page systemctl(1) line 561 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K           absolute paths to unit files (in which case these files are read directly). If a[m
[7m Manual page systemctl(1) line 562 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K           specified unit file is located outside of the usual unit file directories, an[m
           additional symlink is created, linking it into the unit configuration path, thus[m
           ensuring it is found when requested by commands such as [1mstart[22m. The file system where[m
           the linked unit files are located must be accessible when systemd is started (e.g.[m
           anything underneath /home/ or /var/ is not allowed, unless those directories are[m
           located on the root file system).[m
[m
           This command will print the file system operations executed. This output may be[m
           suppressed by passing [1m--quiet[22m.[m
[m
           Note that this operation creates only the symlinks suggested in the [Install] section[m
           of the unit files. While this command is the recommended way to manipulate the unit[m
           configuration directory, the administrator is free to make additional changes[m
           manually by placing or removing symlinks below this directory. This is particularly[m
[7m Manual page systemctl(1) line 576 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K           useful to create configurations that deviate from the suggested default installation.[m
           In this case, the administrator must make sure to invoke [1mdaemon-reload [22mmanually as[m
           necessary, in order to ensure the changes are taken into account.[m
[m
           When using this operation on units without install information, a warning about it is[m
           shown.  [1m--no-warn [22mcan be used to suppress the warning.[m
[m
           Enabling units should not be confused with starting (activating) units, as done by[m
           the [1mstart [22mcommand. Enabling and starting units is orthogonal: units may be [7menable[27m[22md[m
           without being started and started without being [7menable[27md. Enabling simply hooks the[m
           unit into various suggested places (for example, so that the unit is automatically[m
           started on boot or when a particular kind of hardware is plugged in). Starting[m
           actually spawns the daemon process (in case of service units), or binds the socket[m
           (in case of socket units), and so on.[m
[7m Manual page systemctl(1) line 590 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K[m
           Depending on whether [1m--system[22m, [1m--user[22m, [1m--runtime[22m, or [1m--global [22mis specified, this[m
           [7menable[27ms the unit for the system, for the calling user only, for only this boot of the[m
           system, or for all future logins of all users. Note that in the last case, no systemd[m
           daemon configuration is reloaded.[m
[m
           Using [1m[7menable[27m[1m [22mon masked units is not supported and results in an error.[m
[m
       [1mdisable [4m[22mUNIT[24m[1m...[0m[m
           Disables one or more units. This removes all symlinks to the unit files backing the[m
           specified units from the unit configuration directory, and hence undoes any changes[m
           made by [1m[7menable[27m[1m [22mor [1mlink[22m. Note that this removes [4mall[24m symlinks to matching unit files,[m
           including manually created symlinks, and not just those actually created by [1m[7menable[27m[1m [22mor[m
           [1mlink[22m. Note that while [1mdisable [22mundoes the effect of [1m[7menable[27m[22m, the two commands are[m
[7m Manual page systemctl(1) line 604 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K           otherwise not symmetric, as [1mdisable [22mmay remove more symlinks than a prior [1m[7menable[27m[m
           invocation of the same unit created.[m
[m
           This command expects valid unit names only, it does not accept paths to unit files.[m
[m
           In addition to the units specified as arguments, all units are disabled that are[m
           listed in the [4mAlso=[24m setting contained in the [Install] section of any of the unit[m
           files being operated on.[m
[m
           This command implicitly reloads the system manager configuration after completing the[m
           operation. Note that this command does not implicitly stop the units that are being[m
           disabled. If this is desired, either combine this command with the [1m--now [22mswitch, or[m
           invoke the [1mstop [22mcommand with appropriate arguments later.[m
[m
[7m Manual page systemctl(1) line 618 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K           This command will print information about the file system operations (symlink[m
           removals) executed. This output may be suppressed by passing [1m--quiet[22m.[m
[m
           If a unit gets disabled but its triggering units are still active, a warning[m
           containing the names of the triggering units is shown.  [1m--no-warn [22mcan be used to[m
           suppress the warning.[m
[m
           When this command is used with [1m--user[22m, the units being operated on might still be[m
           [7menable[27md in global scope, and thus get started automatically even after a successful[m
           disablement in user scope. In this case, a warning about it is shown, which can be[m
           suppressed using [1m--no-warn[22m.[m
[m
           This command honors [1m--system[22m, [1m--user[22m, [1m--runtime[22m, [1m--global [22mand [1m--no-warn [22min a similar[m
           way as [1m[7menable[27m[22m.[m
[7m Manual page systemctl(1) line 632 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K[m
           Added in version 238.[m
[m
       [1mre[7menable[27m[1m [4m[22mUNIT[24m[1m...[0m[m
           Re[7menable[27m one or more units, as specified on the command line. This is a combination[m
           of [1mdisable [22mand [1m[7menable[27m[1m [22mand is useful to reset the symlinks a unit file is [7menable[27m[22md with[m
           to the defaults configured in its [Install] section. This command expects a unit name[m
           only, it does not accept paths to unit files.[m
[m
           Added in version 238.[m

           Reset the [7menable[27m/disable status one or more unit files, as specified on the command[m
           line, to the defaults configured in the preset policy files. This has the same effect[m

[1mNAME[0m[m
       systemd.service - Service unit configuration[m
[m
[1mSYNOPSIS[0m[m
       [4mservice[24m.service[m
[m
[1mDESCRIPTION[0m[m
       A unit configuration file whose name ends in ".service" encodes information about a[m
       process controlled and supervised by systemd.[m
[m
       This man page lists the configuration options specific to this unit type. See[m
       [1msystemd.unit[22m(5) for the common options of all unit configuration files. The common[m
       configuration items are configured in the generic [Unit] and [Install] sections. The[m
       service specific configuration options are configured in the [Service] section.[m
[m
       Additional options are listed in [1msystemd.exec[22m(5), which define the execution environment[m
[7m Manual page systemd.service(5) line 1 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K       the commands are executed in, and in [1msystemd.kill[22m(5), which define the way the processes[m
[7m Manual page systemd.service(5) line 2 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K       of the service are terminated, and in [1msystemd.resource-control[22m(5), which configure[m
[7m Manual page systemd.service(5) line 3 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K       resource control settings for the processes of the service.[m
[7m Manual page systemd.service(5) line 4 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K[m
[7m Manual page systemd.service(5) line 5 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K       If SysV init compat is enabled, systemd automatically creates service units that wrap[m
[7m Manual page systemd.service(5) line 6 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K       SysV init scripts (the service name is the same as the name of the script, with a[m
[7m Manual page systemd.service(5) line 7 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K       ".service" suffix added); see [1msystemd-sysv-generator[22m(8).[m
[7m Manual page systemd.service(5) line 8 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K[m

[7m Manual page systemd.service(5) line 10 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K       transiently from the command line.[m

           ‚Ä¢   The [1mexec [22mtype is similar to [1msimple[22m, but the service manager will consider the[m
               unit started immediately after the main service binary has been executed. The[m
               service manager will delay starting of follow-up units until that point. (Or in[m
               other words: [1msimple [22mproceeds with further jobs right after [1mfork() [22mreturns, while[m
               [1mexec [22mwill not proceed before both [1mfork() [22mand [1mexecve() [22min the service process[m
               succeeded.) Note that this means [1msystemctl start [22mcommand lines for [1mexec [22mservices[m
               will report failure when the service's binary cannot be invoked successfully (for[m
               example because the selected [4mUser=[24m doesn't exist, or the service binary is[m
               missing).[m
[m
[7m Manual page systemd.service(5) line 96 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K           ‚Ä¢   If set to [1mforking[22m, the manager will consider the unit started immediately after[m
               the binary that forked off by the manager exits.  [4mThe[24m [4muse[24m [4mof[24m [4mthis[24m [4mtype[24m [4mis[0m[m
               [4mdiscouraged,[24m [4muse[24m [1mnotify[4m[22m,[24m [1mnotify-reload[4m[22m,[24m [4mor[24m [1mdbus [4m[22minstead.[0m[m
[m
               It is expected that the process configured with [4mExecStart=[24m will call [1mfork() [22mas[m
               part of its start-up. The parent process is expected to exit when start-up is[m
               complete and all communication channels are set up. The child continues to run as[m
               the main service process, and the service manager will consider the unit started[m
               when the parent process exits. This is the behavior of traditional UNIX services.[m
               If this setting is used, it is recommended to also use the [4mPIDFile=[24m option, so[m
               that systemd can reliably identify the main process of the service. The manager[m
               will proceed with starting follow-up units after the parent process exits.[m
[m
           ‚Ä¢   Behavior of [1moneshot [22mis similar to [1msimple[22m; however, the service manager will[m
               consider the unit up after the main process exits. It will then start follow-up[m
               units.  [4mRemainAfterExit=[24m is particularly useful for this type of service.[m
               [4mType=[24m[1moneshot [22mis the implied default if neither [4mType=[24m nor [4mExecStart=[24m are[m
               specified. Note that if this option is used without [4mRemainAfterExit=[24m the service[m
[7m Manual page systemd.service(5) line 114 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K               will never enter "active" unit state, but will directly transition from[m
               "activating" to "deactivating" or "dead", since no process is configured that[m
               shall run continuously. In particular this means that after a service of this[m
               type ran (and which has [4mRemainAfterExit=[24m not set) it will not show up as started[m
               afterwards, but as dead.[m
[m
           ‚Ä¢   Behavior of [1mdbus [22mis similar to [1msimple[22m; however, units of this type must have the[m
               [4mBusName=[24m specified and the service manager will consider the unit up when the[m
               specified bus name has been acquired. This type is the default if [4mBusName=[24m is[m
               specified.[m
[m
               Service units with this option configured implicitly gain dependencies on the[m
               dbus.socket unit. A service unit of this type is considered to be in the[m
               activating state until the specified bus name is acquired. It is considered[m
               activated while the bus name is taken. Once the bus name is released the service[m
               is considered being no longer functional which has the effect that the service[m
               manager attempts to terminate any remaining processes belonging to the service.[m
               Services that drop their bus name as part of their shutdown logic thus should be[m
[7m Manual page systemd.service(5) line 132 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K               prepared to receive a [1mSIGTERM [22m(or whichever signal is configured in [4mKillSignal=[24m)[m
               as result.[m
[m
           ‚Ä¢   Behavior of [1mnotify [22mis similar to [1mexec[22m; however, it is expected that the service[m
               sends a "READY=1" notification message via [1msd_notify[22m(3) or an equivalent call[m
               when it has finished starting up. systemd will proceed with starting follow-up[m
               units after this notification message has been sent. If this option is used,[m
               [4mNotifyAccess=[24m (see below) should be set to open access to the notification socket[m
               provided by systemd. If [4mNotifyAccess=[24m is missing or set to [1mnone[22m, it will be[m
               forcibly set to [1mmain[22m.[m
[m
               If the service supports reloading, and uses a signal to start the reload, using[m
               [1mnotify-reload [22minstead is recommended.[m
[m
           ‚Ä¢   Behavior of [1mnotify-reload [22mis similar to [1mnotify[22m, with one difference: the [1mSIGHUP[0m[m
               UNIX process signal is sent to the service's main process when the service is[m
               asked to reload and the manager will wait for a notification about the reload[m
               being finished.[m
[7m Manual page systemd.service(5) line 150 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K[m
               When initiating the reload process the service is expected to reply with a[m
               notification message via [1msd_notify[22m(3) that contains the "RELOADING=1" field in[m
               combination with "MONOTONIC_USEC=" set to the current monotonic time (i.e.[m
               [1mCLOCK_MONOTONIC [22min [1mclock_gettime[22m(2)) in Œºs, formatted as decimal string. Once[m
               reloading is complete another notification message must be sent, containing[m
               "READY=1". Using this service type and implementing this reload protocol is an[m
               efficient alternative to providing an [4mExecReload=[24m command for reloading of the[m
               service's configuration.[m
[m
               The signal to send can be tweaked via [4mReloadSignal=[24m, see below.[m
[m
           ‚Ä¢   Behavior of [1midle [22mis very similar to [1msimple[22m; however, actual execution of the[m
               service program is delayed until all active jobs are dispatched. This may be used[m
               to avoid interleaving of output of shell services with the status output on the[m
               console. Note that this type is useful only to improve console output, it is not[m
               useful as a general unit ordering tool, and the effect of this service type is[m
               subject to a 5s timeout, after which the service program is invoked anyway.[m
[7m Manual page systemd.service(5) line 168 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K[m
           It is recommended to use [4mType=[24m[1mexec [22mfor long-running services, as it ensures that[m
           process setup errors (e.g. errors such as a missing service executable, or missing[m
           user) are properly tracked. However, as this service type won't propagate the[m
           failures in the service's own startup code (as opposed to failures in the preparatory[m
           steps the service manager executes before [1mexecve()[22m) and doesn't allow ordering of[m
           other units against completion of initialization of the service code itself (which[m
           for example is useful if clients need to connect to the service through some form of[m
           IPC, and the IPC channel is only established by the service itself ‚Äî in contrast to[m
           doing this ahead of time through socket or bus activation or similar), it might not[m
           be sufficient for many cases. If so, [1mnotify[22m, [1mnotify-reload[22m, or [1mdbus [22m(the latter only[m
           in case the service provides a D-Bus interface) are the preferred options as they[m
           allow service program code to precisely schedule when to consider the service started[m
           up successfully and when to proceed with follow-up units. The [1mnotify[22m/[1mnotify-reload[0m[m
           service types require explicit support in the service codebase (as [1msd_notify() [22mor an[m
           equivalent API needs to be invoked by the service at the appropriate time) ‚Äî if it's[m
           not supported, then [1mforking [22mis an alternative: it supports the traditional[m
           heavy-weight UNIX service start-up protocol. Note that using any type other than[m
[7m Manual page systemd.service(5) line 186 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K           [1msimple [22mpossibly delays the boot process, as the service manager needs to wait for at[m
           least some service initialization to complete. (Also note it is generally not[m
           recommended to use [1midle [22mor [1moneshot [22mfor long-running services.)[m
[m
           Note that various service settings (e.g.  [4mUser=[24m, [4mGroup=[24m through libc NSS) might[m
           result in "hidden" blocking IPC calls to other services when used. Sometimes it might[m
           be advisable to use the [1msimple [22mservice type to ensure that the service manager's[m
           transaction logic is not affected by such potentially slow operations and hidden[m
           dependencies, as this is the only service type where the service manager will not[m
           wait for such service execution setup operations to complete before proceeding.[m
[m
       [4mExitType=[0m[m
           Specifies when the manager should consider the service to be finished. One of [1mmain [22mor[m
           [1mcgroup[22m:[m
[m
           ‚Ä¢   If set to [1mmain [22m(the default), the service manager will consider the unit stopped[m
               when the main process, which is determined according to the [4mType=[24m, exits.[m
               Consequently, it cannot be used with [4mType=[24m[1moneshot[22m.[m
[7m Manual page systemd.service(5) line 204 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K[m
           ‚Ä¢   If set to [1mcgroup[22m, the service will be considered running as long as at least one[m
               process in the cgroup has not exited.[m
[m
           It is generally recommended to use [4mExitType=[24m[1mmain [22mwhen a service has a known forking[m
           model and a main process can reliably be determined.  [4mExitType=[24m [1mcgroup [22mis meant for[m
           applications whose forking model is not known ahead of time and which might not have[m
           a specific main process. It is well suited for transient or automatically generated[m
           services, such as graphical applications inside of a desktop environment.[m
[m
           Added in version 250.[m
[m
       [4mRemainAfterExit=[0m[m
           Takes a boolean value that specifies whether the service shall be considered active[m
           even when all its processes exited. Defaults to [1mno[22m.[m
[m
       [4mGuessMainPID=[0m[m
           Takes a boolean value that specifies whether systemd should try to guess the main PID[m
[7m Manual page systemd.service(5) line 222 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K           of a service if it cannot be determined reliably. This option is ignored unless[m
           [1mType=forking [22mis set and [1mPIDFile= [22mis unset because for the other types or with an[m
           explicitly configured PID file, the main PID is always known. The guessing algorithm[m
           might come to incorrect conclusions if a daemon consists of more than one process. If[m
           the main PID cannot be determined, failure detection and automatic restarting of a[m
           service will not work reliably. Defaults to [1myes[22m.[m
[m
       [4mPIDFile=[0m[m
           Takes a path referring to the PID file of the service. Usage of this option is[m
           recommended for services where [4mType=[24m is set to [1mforking[22m. The path specified typically[m
           points to a file below /run/. If a relative path is specified it is hence prefixed[m
           with /run/. The service manager will read the PID of the main process of the service[m
           from this file after start-up of the service. The service manager will not write to[m
           the file configured here, although it will remove the file after the service has shut[m
           down if it still exists. The PID file does not need to be owned by a privileged user,[m
           but if it is owned by an unprivileged user additional safety restrictions are[m
           enforced: the file may not be a symlink to a file owned by a different user (neither[m
           directly nor indirectly), and the PID file must refer to a process already belonging[m
[7m Manual page systemd.service(5) line 240 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K           to the service.[m
[m
           Note that PID files should be avoided in modern projects. Use [1mType=notify[22m,[m
           [1mType=notify-reload [22mor [1mType=simple [22mwhere possible, which does not require use of PID[m
           files to determine the main process of a service and avoids needless forking.[m
[m
       [4mBusName=[0m[m
           Takes a D-Bus destination name that this service shall use. This option is mandatory[m
           for services where [4mType=[24m is set to [1mdbus[22m. It is recommended to always set this[m
           property if known to make it easy to map the service name to the D-Bus destination.[m
           In particular, [1msystemctl service-log-level/service-log-target [22mverbs make use of this.[m
[m
       [4mExecStart=[0m[m
           Commands that are executed when this service is started. The value is split into zero[m
           or more command lines according to the rules described in the section "Command Lines"[m
           below.[m
[m
           Unless [4mType=[24m is [1moneshot[22m, exactly one command must be given. When [4mType=oneshot[24m is[m
[7m Manual page systemd.service(5) line 258 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K           used, zero or more commands may be specified. Commands may be specified by providing[m
           multiple command lines in the same directive, or alternatively, this directive may be[m
           specified more than once with the same effect. If the empty string is assigned to[m
           this option, the list of commands to start is reset, prior assignments of this option[m
           will have no effect. If no [4mExecStart=[24m is specified, then the service must have[m
           [4mRemainAfterExit=yes[24m and at least one [4mExecStop=[24m line set. (Services lacking both[m
           [4mExecStart=[24m and [4mExecStop=[24m are not valid.)[m
[m
           If more than one command is specified, the commands are invoked sequentially in the[m
           order they appear in the unit file. If one of the commands fails (and is not prefixed[m
           with "-"), other lines are not executed, and the unit is considered failed.[m
[m
           Unless [4mType=forking[24m is set, the process started via this command line will be[m
           considered the main process of the daemon.[m
[m
       [4mExecStartPre=[24m, [4mExecStartPost=[0m[m
           Additional commands that are executed before or after the command in [4mExecStart=[24m,[m
           respectively. Syntax is the same as for [4mExecStart=[24m, except that multiple command[m
